    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7046724574713286921">"Der Richter und sein Henker" ist einer seiner berühmtesten Romane - die Geschichte eines Mordes. Mit den reißerischen Mitteln einer Detektivstory erzählt er die Aufklärung einer Gewalttat an einem Polizeileutnant, den letzten Fall des totkranken Komissars Bärlach - die Geschichte einer hintergründigen Pointe.</span>

<div id="review_2021829396" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021829396" />
    <a title="Glenn Russell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23385697-glenn-russell"><img alt="Glenn Russell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505195595p2/23385697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021829396?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glenn Russell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glenn Russell" href="/user/show/23385697-glenn-russell">Glenn Russell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780224611893" href="/book/show/510658.The_Judge_and_His_Hangman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021829396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5382571381316104732"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496846811i/22958673._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>"The difference between humans and wild animals is that humans pray before they commit murder."<br/>-Friedrich Dürrenmatt (1921-1990), Swiss novelist and dramatist<br/><br/>In his short review of this extraordinary novel, my good friend Mark Hebwood from London wrote: "Loved it! This is a bit like taking the essence of detective novels and distilling it down to concentrate. Great plot, excellent twists, and great finale. I immediately bought all other detective novels he wrote."<br/><br/>Thanks, Mark! Likewise, all Frie</span>
  <span id="freeText5382571381316104732" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496846811i/22958673._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>"The difference between humans and wild animals is that humans pray before they commit murder."<br>-Friedrich Dürrenmatt (1921-1990), Swiss novelist and dramatist<br><br>In his short review of this extraordinary novel, my good friend Mark Hebwood from London wrote: "Loved it! This is a bit like taking the essence of detective novels and distilling it down to concentrate. Great plot, excellent twists, and great finale. I immediately bought all other detective novels he wrote."<br><br>Thanks, Mark! Likewise, all Friedrich Dürrenmatt detective novels are now on my to-be-read list. And I’m not usually a fan of detective mysteries, to say the least - other than a handful of those old classics like Chandler’s <i>The Big Sleep</i> and Hammett’s <i>The Thin Man</i>, no dick fiction for me, thank you. But I am a big fan of tight, penetrating existential novels such as <i>The Stranger</i> and <i>Nausea</i>, and, let me tell you, <i>The Judge and His Hangman</i> is every bit as tight and as penetrating and as existential as these two French classics. <br><br>To say anything about plot more than a brief sketch would be to say too much since nearly every page contains subtle turns and developments that will keep a reader mesmerized from beginning to end. And that’s not overstatement as I’m not the only one to pass such a glowing judgement - literary critic and acclaimed author, Kay Boyle, likewise wrote how this Swiss novel holds the reader mesmerized. Usually I take my time with a novel but once I read the first page of <i>The Judge and His Hangman</i> I was hooked – I finished its one hundred pages in one evening, in one sitting. <br><br>Anyway, Friedrich Dürrenmatt’s work features old, stogy, fatally ill Commissioner Barlach working on the case of a murdered police officer. The location is in Switzerland, in and around the capital of Berne. There is an element of political intrigue; there’s tension between new school criminology and old-school, small town Barlach; there’s a string of intriguing characters, including a pompous Congressman-Colonel, a bureaucratic chief of police and, one of my personal favorites, a novelist. But, above all, there is the philosophic: the battle of good versus evil, nihilism versus any moral sense, and what it means to live an authentic human life. An absolute must read for anyone attracted to either existentialism or detective novels.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496851818i/22959297._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Berne, Switzerland, location of this Friedrich Dürrenmatt novel published in 1950</span>
  <a data-text-id="5382571381316104732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_124966041" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124966041" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124966041?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780224611893" href="/book/show/510658.The_Judge_and_His_Hangman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=1001-book">1001-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=german">german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=switzerland">switzerland</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124966041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17604338377181836484">519. Der Richter und sein Henker = The Judge and His Hangman, Friedrich Dürrenmatt<br/><br/>The Judge and His Hangman is a 1950 novel by the Swiss writer Friedrich Dürrenmatt. It was first published in English in 1954, in a translation by Cyrus Brooks and later in a translation by Therese Pol. A new translation by Joel Agee appeared in 2006, published together with its sequel Suspicion, as The Inspector Bärlach Mysteries, with a foreword by Sven Birkerts. Together with Dürrenmatt's The Pledge: Requiem for</span>
  <span id="freeText17604338377181836484" style="display:none">519. Der Richter und sein Henker = The Judge and His Hangman, Friedrich Dürrenmatt<br /><br />The Judge and His Hangman is a 1950 novel by the Swiss writer Friedrich Dürrenmatt. It was first published in English in 1954, in a translation by Cyrus Brooks and later in a translation by Therese Pol. A new translation by Joel Agee appeared in 2006, published together with its sequel Suspicion, as The Inspector Bärlach Mysteries, with a foreword by Sven Birkerts. Together with Dürrenmatt's The Pledge: Requiem for the Detective Novel, these stories are considered classics of crime fiction, fusing existential philosophy and the detective genre.<br /><br />قاضی و جلادش - فردریش دورنمات ؛ انتشارات: (جمال الحق، ماهی) ادبیات آلمان؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و هشتم ماه اکتبر سال 2012 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: قاضی و جلادش؛ نویسنده: فریدریش دورنمات؛ مترجم: محمود حسینی زاد؛ تهران، جمال الحق؛ 1371؛ در 132 ص، مصور؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، ماهی، 1386؛ شابک 9647848891؛ چاپ سوم 1389؛ چهارم 1392؛ شابک 9789647848890؛<br /><br />جسدی در حاشیه‌ ی جاده‌ ای خارج از شهر کشف شده، که خیلی زود مشخص می‌شود، جسد سروان «اشمید»، افسر جوان پلیس «برن» است؛ از آن پس، باید در انتظار سرنخ‌هایی برای کشف راز قتل باشیم، اما طولی نمی‌کشد که خوانشگر درمی‌یابد، قتل تنها تکه‌ ای از پازلی بزرگ و پیچیده است؛ کارآگاه «برلاخ»، بازرس پیر، و کارکشته‌ ی اداره‌ ی پلیس، که رییس «اشمید» هم هست، در مرکز داستان قرار دارد. برلاخ، در جوانی، ده سال مستشار اداره‌ ی پلیس استانبول بوده، روزی در میخانه‌ ای، شرطی با یک مرد می‌بندد، که سرگذشت هر دو را تغییر، و به مسیر تازه‌ ای می‌اندازد. برلاخ می‌گوید «جنایت حماقت است»، و دست همه‌ ی قاتل‌ها سرانجام رو می‌شود. مرد اما، شیفته‌ ی ذکاوت، و تیزهوشی خویش است، و آن سخن را باور ندارد. شرط می‌بندد، جنایاتی خواهد کرد، که پنهان خواهند ماند. او، پیش چشمان برلاخ، تاجری را به رودخانه می‌اندازد، اما با زیرکی ثابت می‌کند، که این رخداد خودکشی بوده، و از عدالت می‌گریزد. این بازی چهل سال آزگار، ادامه می‌یابد، و دستگیری قاتل، و اثبات جنایت او، بزرگ‌ترین آرزوی برلاخ می‌شود. در واقع، نقص قانون، و عجز آن از برقراری کامل عدالت، یکی از بن‌ مایه‌ های اصلی رمان است. دورنمات این موتیف را در رمان‌های دیگرش هم پی می‌گیرد، آن‌جا که دست برلاخ، برای اقدام قانونی، علیه «امن‌ برگر» بسته است، در رمان «سو‌ء‌ ظن» و یا وقتی «ماتئی» با مشکلی مشابه مواجه می‌شود، در رمان «قول». قانون گاه، برخلاف فلسفه‌ اش، کارکردی ضدعدالت می‌یابد، و خلاءهایی دارد، که ظالمان و جانیان را، در فرار از عدالت یاری می‌کند؛ این موضوعی‌ ست، که دورنمات، در ضمن روایت نفس‌گیر و عالی خود، بر آن انگشت می‌گذارد، و به‌ طور غیرمستقیم از آن انتقاد می‌کند. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="17604338377181836484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2864004522" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2864004522" />
    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36555254-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536187488p2/36555254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2864004522?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/36555254-robin">Robin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Classy broads and dames (and those who love them)</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Robin by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/73768036-lark-benobi">lark benobi</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=1001-before-you-die">1001-before-you-die</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=noir">noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=switzerland">switzerland</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2864004522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14234980614920253394">I think I'm going to make up a new sub-genre. I'm going to call that sub-genre <b>"classy noir"</b>. And I'm going to slap that label right on the front cover of this fantastic 1952 novella.<br/><br/>It's SO classy. No shabby P.I. leering at the "assets" of a bodacious blonde (I'm lookin' at YOU Raymond Chandler). No one gets hit with a "sap" (Chandler loves the sap). No one drinks themselves into oblivion alongside their half naked girlfriend like a couple of shameless barflies night after night (you know who y</span>
  <span id="freeText14234980614920253394" style="display:none">I think I'm going to make up a new sub-genre. I'm going to call that sub-genre <b>"classy noir"</b>. And I'm going to slap that label right on the front cover of this fantastic 1952 novella.<br /><br />It's SO classy. No shabby P.I. leering at the "assets" of a bodacious blonde (I'm lookin' at YOU Raymond Chandler). No one gets hit with a "sap" (Chandler loves the sap). No one drinks themselves into oblivion alongside their half naked girlfriend like a couple of shameless barflies night after night (you know who you are, Charles Willeford).<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I love Chandler and his amazing similes. But Swiss writer Friedrich Dürrenmatt does something here to noir which makes it a lot less pulpy and "Pop Art", and turns it into something deep, subtle, and existential-as-fuck.<br /><br />I know what you're thinking - Robin, "classy noir" doesn't sounds like much fun! <br /><br />Oh, but it is. Striking and original, <i>The Judge and His Hangman</i> laughs in the face of the traditional detective novel. Inspector Barlach, elderly and deathly ill, refuses to hunt for clues and then analyze à la Poirot, until the last puzzle piece fits in its just and proper place. That Golden-Age fantasy doesn't fit into Barlach's grim life. Refusing to apply science and logic to his investigation, Barlach is inscrutable, tortured, and he never locks his front door.<br /><br />The combination of powerful prose, artful plot, an arch-enemy of Moriarty calibre, and a standoff in a darkened apartment between two armed men, served to keep me completely glued to the page. The currents run deep here. It's as much about the unpredictability of human nature and the spell and riddle of evil, as it is about whodunnit.<br /><br />But it's also a thrilling mystery, and you'll have to wait until the end to find out who is the judge and who is the executioner. See? Classic, AND <i>classy</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14234980614920253394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1756219877" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756219877" />
    <a title="Greg Brozeit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26552534-greg-brozeit"><img alt="Greg Brozeit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544324486p2/26552534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756219877?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg Brozeit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg Brozeit" href="/user/show/26552534-greg-brozeit">Greg Brozeit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/31271462-der-richter-und-sein-henker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26552534-greg-brozeit?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26552534-greg-brozeit?shelf=deutsch">deutsch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26552534-greg-brozeit?shelf=d%C3%BCrrenmatt">dürrenmatt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756219877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14666329992149459920">This is a perfect novella. Dürrenmatt wrote <i>The Judge and his Executioner</i> around the same time as the play <i>The Marriage of Mr. Mississippi</i>. Both stories revolve around the theme of two antagonists who are reunited by circumstances that occurred decades apart.<br/><br/>In 1948 a colleague of Swiss police inspector Bärlach is found murdered, shot and hunched over the steering wheel of his car on a rural highway in the Alps. As he takes up the case, Bärlach is near the end of his career and has a year to liv</span>
  <span id="freeText14666329992149459920" style="display:none">This is a perfect novella. Dürrenmatt wrote <i>The Judge and his Executioner</i> around the same time as the play <i>The Marriage of Mr. Mississippi</i>. Both stories revolve around the theme of two antagonists who are reunited by circumstances that occurred decades apart.<br /><br />In 1948 a colleague of Swiss police inspector Bärlach is found murdered, shot and hunched over the steering wheel of his car on a rural highway in the Alps. As he takes up the case, Bärlach is near the end of his career and has a year to live because of illness. He worked a number of years in Turkey and then in Frankfurt, Germany, where he was forced to leave in 1933 after slapping a superior officer who was a Nazi. His grizzled wisdom is hidden behind a curtain of an unorthodox lifestyle and seemingly lax work habits.<br /><br />His path crosses with a man he met 40 years earlier in Istanbul. One believes in his criminal genius, which is borne out by his political power. The other devotes his life to fighting crime. When they meet again, it seems that Bärlach is the loser.<br /><br /><i>The Judge and his Executioner</i> seems, for most part, a compact, tense crime-noir novel. Even after we think we’ve come to the conclusion, Dürrenmatt upends it all in the final ten pages when we realize that it’s all a complex human chess game in which he is the grand master. This is classic Dürrenmatt where nothing is as it seems and the ending leaves indelible memories that cause multiple re-readings of selected passages once we know how it will end. Knowing the ending just makes them better. That plus his asides on Swiss culture make it a real treat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14666329992149459920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2720252946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9856379116134038416">Generally I do not like the detective genre that much, but Dürrenmatt in this little book plays a nice game with the reader: it is unclear to the end who is judge and who is executioner. And he also likes to jump over the boundaries of the classic detective story: of course suspense is all around and keeps the attention going, but philosophical side-paths are also regularly followed, especially because the main suspect is the personification of the nihilistic evil. Occasionally the style was a b</span>
  <span id="freeText9856379116134038416" style="display:none">Generally I do not like the detective genre that much, but Dürrenmatt in this little book plays a nice game with the reader: it is unclear to the end who is judge and who is executioner. And he also likes to jump over the boundaries of the classic detective story: of course suspense is all around and keeps the attention going, but philosophical side-paths are also regularly followed, especially because the main suspect is the personification of the nihilistic evil. Occasionally the style was a bit too imaginative (his description of threatening natural phenomena even reminded me of Dutch author Couperus), and the bet on which the intrigue rests, is perhaps a little far-fetched, but all in all this is a nice story. The self-willed inspector Bärlach is a worthy participant in the category of Holmes, Poirot and Maigret; only, I am not sure whether I would qualify him as a judge or as a hangman, and also that ambiguity adorns Dürrenmatt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9856379116134038416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780224611893" href="/book/show/510658.The_Judge_and_His_Hangman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/637062-jacob?shelf=fiction-and-literature">fiction-and-literature</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer702997175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6162501049569431111">Many years ago in Istanbul, two men made a wager--one, that criminals always pay; the other, that he could get away with anything. Forty years later, in Switzerland, a young police officer is murdered, and Inspector Berlach finds he has one last chance to catch Gastmann, the one that got away. <br/><br/>Many good books are just the right length, but there are some out there that deserve to be longer. This is both. As a brief, well-plotted mystery novella detailing the end of one man's forty-year pursuit o</span>
  <span id="freeText6162501049569431111" style="display:none">Many years ago in Istanbul, two men made a wager--one, that criminals always pay; the other, that he could get away with anything. Forty years later, in Switzerland, a young police officer is murdered, and Inspector Berlach finds he has one last chance to catch Gastmann, the one that got away. <br /><br />Many good books are just the right length, but there are some out there that deserve to be longer. This is both. As a brief, well-plotted mystery novella detailing the end of one man's forty-year pursuit of a criminal, <i>The Judge and His Hangman</i> (<i>Der Richter und sein Henker</i> in German) is pretty damn good--but those (like me) hoping to read more of that first encounter in Istanbul and the forty years in between may find that this book is too short by several hundred pages, at least. Too short--or the right length? <br /><br />Both, probably. It's up to you to decide. Me, I think I'll try <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_D%C3%BCrrenmatt" rel="nofollow noopener">Friedrich Dürrenmatt's</a> other work. His story <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tunnel_(short_story)" rel="nofollow noopener">"The Tunnel"</a> sounds rather promising.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6162501049569431111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5997164010981678841">Terrifically entertaining. A good first novel for those studying German who are ready to tackle something longer. I have a copy published in the 50's where the publisher compared Dürrenmatt's style to G.K. Chesterton and Graham Greene, which at first seemed strange (since these three authors seem very dissimilar to me) but on reflection they all employ a subtle, wry humor that makes their sentences and meanings land in unexpected ways. </span>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2368152896162365605">I will certainly read the other crime novels penned by Durrenmatt, but I found this one a bit dry and unemotional. An inspector who knows the killer from page 1 and just waits for the truth to shine? To me not exactly convincing. However, the writing is exceptional, and what it lacks in plot, it gains in witty and cynical remarks and a bit of beautiful scenery. Whoever makes a sleepy Swiss village atmospheric, surely deserves our recognition! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Col" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Col" href="/user/show/12761919-col">Col</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782273417" href="/book/show/34379486-the-judge-and-his-hangman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12761919-col?shelf=d">d</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12761919-col?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2071354004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15474702452380535392">Synopsis/blurb.....<br/><br/>Inspector Barlach is dying. But not fast enough for his arch-enemy<br/><br/>When a member of the Bern police force is shot dead on a Swiss country road, the enigmatic Inspector Barlach and his colleague Tschanz are intent on tracking down the killer. But the ailing Inspector doesn't have time to lose. Soon the pair discover that the victim was murdered on his way to a clandestine party at the home of a wealthy power broker - so why was a local policeman socialising with some of Switzerl</span>
  <span id="freeText15474702452380535392" style="display:none">Synopsis/blurb.....<br /><br />Inspector Barlach is dying. But not fast enough for his arch-enemy<br /><br />When a member of the Bern police force is shot dead on a Swiss country road, the enigmatic Inspector Barlach and his colleague Tschanz are intent on tracking down the killer. But the ailing Inspector doesn't have time to lose. Soon the pair discover that the victim was murdered on his way to a clandestine party at the home of a wealthy power broker - so why was a local policeman socialising with some of Switzerland's most influential men? Who was his shadowy host? And why has Barlach's past returned to haunt him in his final hours?<br /><br />The Judge and His Hangman is a thrilling tale of lifelong rivalry, and of two men chained together by a wager that would destroy them both.<br /><br />Friedrich Dürrenmatt (1921-1990) was a Swiss author and dramatist, most famous for his plays The Visit and The Physicists, which earned him a reputation as one of the greatest playwrights in the German language. He also wrote four highly regarded crime novels: The Pledge (adapted for a 2001 film starring Jack Nicholson), Suspicion and The Execution of Justice, are also published by Pushkin Vertigo.<br />-------------------------<br />My take.....<br /><br />My second time with Swiss author Friedrich Durrenmatt after enjoying The Pledge earlier this year. Thoughts here.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://col2910.blogspot.co.uk/2017/05/friedrich-durrenmatt-pledge-1958.html">http://col2910.blogspot.co.uk/2017/05...</a><br /><br />This re-issue from Pushkin Vertigo is a slim offering at 128 pages long, but for my reading tastes the length is a plus. The murder of a policeman and the subsequent investigation is interesting though it takes us until over halfway to discover in fact that there is more going on than meets the eye.<br /><br />Inspector Barlach is and has been battling a foe for over forty years, unsuccessfully thus far. He has a last opportunity to bring him down, before his own ill health does for him.<br /><br />I liked Barlach as a character - his solitude, his methods, his irritation with his superior and his clever manipulations, orchestrating events and people like a puppet master to achieve the desired outcome. More than one way to skin a cat.<br /><br />I'm not usually a massive fan of older books (pre-early 60s is where I draw the line), I'll happily make an exception for Durrenmatt.<br /><br />A few more from him sit on the pile - The Visit, The Quarry, The Execution of Justice, Suspicion.<br /><br />4 from 5<br /><br />Read in August, 2017<br />Published 1954 originally (2017 re-issue from Pushkin Vertigo)<br />Page count - 128<br />Source - review copy from publisher<br />Format - paperback<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://col2910.blogspot.co.uk/2017/08/friedrich-durrenmatt-judge-and-his.html">https://col2910.blogspot.co.uk/2017/0...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15474702452380535392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=mid-20th-century">mid-20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=1001-books">1001-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer244142730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12055277544273185502">Such a good, satisfying read! It doesn't matter that it is blink-of-the-eye short. Of course I picked this up knowing it is a mystery novel, and although the murder is discovered on the first page, I almost didn't feel as if I should be trying to solve it alongside Inspector Barlach. Barlach knows things we don't, unlike many detectives in other novels. The specific details of what he knows aren't ever revealed, but the core of what he knows is peeled back so that we see the dirty underneath.<br/><br/>Dür</span>
  <span id="freeText12055277544273185502" style="display:none">Such a good, satisfying read! It doesn't matter that it is blink-of-the-eye short. Of course I picked this up knowing it is a mystery novel, and although the murder is discovered on the first page, I almost didn't feel as if I should be trying to solve it alongside Inspector Barlach. Barlach knows things we don't, unlike many detectives in other novels. The specific details of what he knows aren't ever revealed, but the core of what he knows is peeled back so that we see the dirty underneath.<br /><br />Dürrenmatt's prose isn't literary fiction, but assuming the translation is not better than the original German, this is better than typical prose for the mystery genre. Dürrenmatt gained fame as a playwright and his ability to create scenes is evident. I quite liked the visuals presented through his writing. The Barlach characterization is quite good. If I were to describe the lesser characterizations as caricatures, I would be selling them short. Still, they aren't fully drawn and it would be an exaggeration to say so.<br /><br />I'm sorry that it appears there is only one other novel with Inspector Barlach, but I think there are a couple more mysteries by this author. I look forward to stumbling across them. This deserves the full 4-stars I award for the genre, and it sits toward the top of that pile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12055277544273185502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2589787680" />
    <a title="Andy Weston" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston"><img alt="Andy Weston" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190073185p2/313206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2589787680?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Weston" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Weston" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston">Andy Weston</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780224611893" href="/book/show/510658.The_Judge_and_His_Hangman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=switzerland">switzerland</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2589787680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer785100741187295390">Friedrich Dürrenmatt (Swiss) was primarily known as a playwrite, but wrote several philosophical crime thrillers in which he stamped his own unique mark of how he saw the genre. He had a deep dislike for the predictable plot and formulaic structure of the detective novel. <br/>I’ve only read two of his books, but I prefer this to his more famous <i> The Pledge </i>, probably more well-known as a corrupted version of it went on to be two successful films. <br/>This is the first of his Inspector Barlach novels, an</span>
  <span id="freeText785100741187295390" style="display:none">Friedrich Dürrenmatt (Swiss) was primarily known as a playwrite, but wrote several philosophical crime thrillers in which he stamped his own unique mark of how he saw the genre. He had a deep dislike for the predictable plot and formulaic structure of the detective novel. <br />I’ve only read two of his books, but I prefer this to his more famous <i> The Pledge </i>, probably more well-known as a corrupted version of it went on to be two successful films. <br />This is the first of his Inspector Barlach novels, and it is his character that gives the strength to this short read. Barlach is at the end of his career, and has just been diagnosed with a terminal illness. He has never done things by convention and through results is solving cases he has been given some leeway, but after his diagnosis he sees the opportunity to do battle with an adversary whom he was never able to bring to justice. <br />It’s a short and rewarding read, and leaves you wanting more from Barlach. It’s a real skill to portray such convincing characters in such few pages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="785100741187295390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9402309034465104646">The story glitters with a cutting intelligence bared as the story unfolds. A policeman has been murdered and solving the crime throws up enough questions, twists, moral conundrums, social observations to have made this a 1000 page book. All the more remarkable that in Durrenmatts masterful hands it is covered in 90 or so pages. Also written in the sort of simple German that makes it extremely easy for those whom German is a second language to understand.</span>

<div id="review_2764784708" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2764784708" />
    <a title="Seth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4351439-seth"><img alt="Seth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319242813p2/4351439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2764784708?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth" href="/user/show/4351439-seth">Seth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/31271462-der-richter-und-sein-henker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4351439-seth?shelf=german-literature">german-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2764784708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12627997062364283082">Friedrich Dürrenmatt was one of Switzerland’s leading writer-intellectuals, along with Max Frisch and much earlier Gottfried Keller. After studying art history, German literature, philosophy, and the natural sciences at the University of Basel, Dürrenmatt decided to pursue writing as a career and painting as an avocation. <br/><br/>Dürrenmatt is known not only for his plays, including The Visit (Der Besuch der alten Dame) and The Physicists (Die Physiker), but also for his detective novels, of which The J</span>
  <span id="freeText12627997062364283082" style="display:none">Friedrich Dürrenmatt was one of Switzerland’s leading writer-intellectuals, along with Max Frisch and much earlier Gottfried Keller. After studying art history, German literature, philosophy, and the natural sciences at the University of Basel, Dürrenmatt decided to pursue writing as a career and painting as an avocation. <br /><br />Dürrenmatt is known not only for his plays, including The Visit (Der Besuch der alten Dame) and The Physicists (Die Physiker), but also for his detective novels, of which The Judge and His Hangman (Der Richter und sein Henker) was the most celebrated. It was adapted into the movie End of the Game, starring Jon Voight and Jacqueline Bisset and with music by Ennio Morricone. <br /><br />Other examples of Dürrenmatt's film impact were The Visit, which featured Ingrid Bergman and Anthony Quinn, and It Happened in Broad Daylight (Es geschah am hellichten Tag), which was based on his novel about a child abduction, The Pledge (Das Versprechen).<br /><br />Dürrenmatt was also outspoken about politics, particularly during the Prague Spring and subsequent Soviet crackdown on Alexander Dubček in 1968. <br /><br />All of this--his writings, artwork, and film impact--are on display at the Dürrenmatt Center in Neuchâtel, which I was pleased to visit recently.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12627997062364283082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120509462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2948651950971160407">Pretty good. Terms such as justice or right are not as clear with Dürrenmatt's detectives as in other stories; chance plays one hell of a role; there are no heroes. Is it nihilistic? I don't know. It's good, though. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('G5O3aOlfsZU/unyfwjdlItzZc+3Pr4do31mIx3mJiSDN/Hslp3oc+aTrI6YBxKEwAthMENd2ILn/oylr9W2ShA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Durch ein Missverständnis, das aufzuklären er den Mut nicht findet, wird er in der Nachbarstadt Goldach seines kostbaren Mantels wegen für einen reichen polnischen Grafen gehalten. Das bürgerliche Trauerspiel kontrastiert die verrottete Moral des Hofes mit der Tugend des Bürgertums. Im Mittelpunkt des Sturm-und-Drang-Stücks steht die tragische Liebesbeziehung zwischen Angehörigen verschiedener Stände: zwischen dem Adligen Ferdinand und der Musikertochter Luise Miller. \'Kabale <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13254294403065229724">Friedrich Dürrenmatt (1921 – 1990) was a Swiss author and dramatist.<br/><br/>Dürrenmatt was born in the Emmental (canton of Bern), the son of a Protestant pastor. His grandfather Ulrich Dürrenmatt was a conservative politician. The family moved to Bern in 1935. Dürrenmatt began to study philosophy and German language and literature at the University of Zurich in 1941, but moved to the University of Bern af</span>
  <span id="freeText13254294403065229724" style="display:none">Friedrich Dürrenmatt (1921 – 1990) was a Swiss author and dramatist.<br /><br />Dürrenmatt was born in the Emmental (canton of Bern), the son of a Protestant pastor. His grandfather Ulrich Dürrenmatt was a conservative politician. The family moved to Bern in 1935. Dürrenmatt began to study philosophy and German language and literature at the University of Zurich in 1941, but moved to the University of Bern after one semester. In 1943 he decided to become an author and dramatist and dropped his academic career. In 1945-46, he wrote his first play, "It is written". On October 11 1946 he married actress Lotti Geissler. She died in 1983 and Dürrenmatt was married again to another actress, Charlotte Kerr, the following year.<br /><br />He was a proponent of epic theater whose plays reflected the recent experiences of World War II. The politically active author gained fame largely due to his avant-garde dramas, philosophically deep crime novels, and often macabre satire. One of his leading sentences was: "A story is not finished, until it has taken the worst turn". Dürrenmatt was a member of the Gruppe Olten.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13254294403065229724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
